<div id="review_162413274" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/162413274" />
    <a title="Wong" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3258366-wong"><img alt="Wong" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1304360163p2/3258366.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/162413274?book_show_action=true">Apr 20, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wong" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wong" href="/user/show/3258366-wong">Wong</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer162413274" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3911296096983122624">Bismillah.<br/><br/>I like books from Jeanne DuPrau. Though her books are intended for younger people, I couldn't help but notice that her books are filled with messages of humanity, peace and the need for us all to break the cycle of hatred. I think that her books suit current situation very well. <br/><br/>I would say that I could agree with 90% of what she's writing in her previous two books. I would definitely ask my future children to read the first two. As for this one, maybe when they are older. <br/><br/>In this book</span>
  <span id="freeText3911296096983122624" style="display:none">Bismillah.<br /><br />I like books from Jeanne DuPrau. Though her books are intended for younger people, I couldn't help but notice that her books are filled with messages of humanity, peace and the need for us all to break the cycle of hatred. I think that her books suit current situation very well. <br /><br />I would say that I could agree with 90% of what she's writing in her previous two books. I would definitely ask my future children to read the first two. As for this one, maybe when they are older. <br /><br />In this book, through allegory, she tried to convey to her readers that there are only two options: 1. There's no God or 2. There are many gods fighting for control. All simply because there are many versions of 'truth' and everyone is claiming that theirs are the true one. <br /><br />I won't agree with that even if you cut my hands. Yes, I am a Muslim.<br /><br />Religion it seems, for DuPrau, is a list of rules that are unbendable, rigid and limiting. Religion, for me is a collection of principals, that can be bent according to situation. As in Islam, there is no specific things say on how to rule a government. But there are certain principals that must be fulfilled for a government to be considered 'Good government'.<br /><br />Though may be unintentional on her part, it seems clear to me that any flaws in the followers of a religion shouldn't be attributed to a religion as a weakness.<br /><br />Yet I commend her work as entertaining and full of good messages. For instance the danger of religious fanaticism, forgiveness, thirst for knowledge and how rationality may (a big may) be used to gauge what is evil and what is good.<br /><br />I honestly think that secularism is not the answer to our human condition. I've established within myself that there is God. And I have in my consciousness, that if there is God, there must be some sort of guidance for us in this world. And I find the Quran and the Hadith a perfect guidance for mankind.<br /><br />Allahua'lam.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3911296096983122624" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1133812721?book_show_action=true">Dec 16, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Olivia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Olivia" href="/user/show/4682653-olivia">Olivia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4682653-olivia?shelf=sucky-books">sucky-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4682653-olivia?shelf=dystopian-utopian">dystopian-utopian</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1133812721" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3845195687945151688">*sigh* why do I do this to myself? I saw the multitude of 1-star ratings...I considered them...and I chose to read this travesty of a book anyway. Uuuuuhhhh...<br/>GOODREADS FRIENDS, DO NOT REPEAT MY MISTAKE!<br/>I don't know what DuPrau was smoking when she wrote this crap, but it wasn't the same awesome stuff that created the first two. This was crap. I skimmed so much of it, after trying really hard to read thoroughly, and I still was able to grasp the basic, ridiculous plot. I didn't even have to try!</span>
  <span id="freeText3845195687945151688" style="display:none">*sigh* why do I do this to myself? I saw the multitude of 1-star ratings...I considered them...and I chose to read this travesty of a book anyway. Uuuuuhhhh...<br />GOODREADS FRIENDS, DO NOT REPEAT MY MISTAKE!<br />I don't know what DuPrau was smoking when she wrote this crap, but it wasn't the same awesome stuff that created the first two. This was crap. I skimmed so much of it, after trying really hard to read thoroughly, and I still was able to grasp the basic, ridiculous plot. I didn't even have to try! There was no excitement, no thrill, no mystery... It's just a girl who comes to temporarily live in a town where religious cultists are using the people. Wow. That certainly doesn't describe a few dozen books. <br />Pretty much, this book is just DuPrau's rant on how people can use religion to hurt others. She doesn't even consider the possibility of good religion. Essentially, by the end, all the bad people are gone, the girl grows up and completes her very generic bucket list (which pretty much included enjoying life and getting married), and Ember is vaguely mentioned on the last page. There is nothing else to know about this novel. <br />It teaches nothing positive (unlike the last two). The characters are incredibly flat and unknowable (unlike the last two). The plot is stale, slow, and has no significant rise or fall (unlike the last two).<br />Pretty much, if you want a good book that has some effort put into it that isn't just an angry person's rant about religion, read the last two.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3845195687945151688" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

The City of Ember and The People of Sparks are much better than this book.<br/><br/>The author does have some nice and believable characters, but the action and drama within the story just fall flat in comparison with her other books. I guess the difficulty is the post-Apocalyptic world of the first two books is extremely compelling, but the pre-Apocalyptic world</span>
  <span id="freeText3053533051366531980" style="display:none">I'll agree with many of the other reviews. This book just isn't up to par with the really amazing stories in the first two books of this series. The City of Ember and The People of Sparks are much better than this book.<br /><br />The author does have some nice and believable characters, but the action and drama within the story just fall flat in comparison with her other books. I guess the difficulty is the post-Apocalyptic world of the first two books is extremely compelling, but the pre-Apocalyptic world in this book just doesn't hold the same potential for an amazing story.<br /><br />If you need 'completeness' in reading a series you can go and read the book, but it's not necessary.<br /><br />Two stars because the writing style is the same very clean youthful story telling, but only 2 stars because the story lacks the compelling nature of the first two books. </span>

<div id="review_1812800519" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1812800519" />
    <a title="Chris Evans" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41096515-chris-evans"><img alt="Chris Evans" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1426030614p2/41096515.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1812800519?book_show_action=true">Nov 17, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chris Evans" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chris Evans" href="/user/show/41096515-chris-evans">Chris Evans</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41096515-chris-evans?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41096515-chris-evans?shelf=trash-don-t-read">trash-don-t-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1812800519" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12450235601205772173">WTF is this? I knew I was in trouble when my suspension of disbelief was shattered on the first page.<br/><br/>Lets start off with the fact that this should NOT be labeled (Book of Ember, #3), this is a (Book of Ember, #0.1) pre-quel/side story.<br/><br/>I'm not sure if Jeanne DuPrau is a terrible writer or a gifted Authorial Troll. The Prophet of Yonwood is an exercise in exquisitely boring story telling. Nothing the two main characters do is of any consequence but Jeanne hangs tantalizing possibilities just out o</span>
  <span id="freeText12450235601205772173" style="display:none">WTF is this? I knew I was in trouble when my suspension of disbelief was shattered on the first page.<br /><br />Lets start off with the fact that this should NOT be labeled (Book of Ember, #3), this is a (Book of Ember, #0.1) pre-quel/side story.<br /><br />I'm not sure if Jeanne DuPrau is a terrible writer or a gifted Authorial Troll. The Prophet of Yonwood is an exercise in exquisitely boring story telling. Nothing the two main characters do is of any consequence but Jeanne hangs tantalizing possibilities just out of reach the whole time.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />The beginning. Some lady has a seizure and goes into a semi-coma. Her friend, a friend who can somehow command the obedience of every powerful official in town, finds her. For no reason at all she not only decides the lady had a vision and is speaking commandments from god, but manages to convince everyone else in town of it. She then goes on a crusade to carry out the none-sense instructions until the lady eventually wakes up and explains what happened.<br /><br />That's it, that's the story. The majority of the story is REALLY REALLY basic and insufferable musings on god and religion. You could skip whole chapters and not miss anything.<br /><br />The worst part about all this is Jeanne teases you with interesting story lines. <br /><br />So the setting is some time in the future right?<br />Not really. It comes across more like a boring version of Pre-Great War Fallout. Everything has a 1940's-ish aesthetic and mentality, but with stupidly over complicated phones and nuclear batteries in some things. No robots, robots would be too interesting.<br /><br />Is this going to be a town dealing with the world ending around it in the cataclysm we know eventually comes? <br />No, that's 50 years in the future. <br /><br />Ooo, there's some paranormal stuff going on with the old Grandfather stuff, are they going to...? <br />No, goes nowhere<br /><br />What about Mr.Hoyt? he's in contact with aliens or extra dimensional beings or something. <br />Never elaborated on, only used as a possible reason the war is postponed for 50 years.<br /><br />What about the fathers cryptic messages?<br />California <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />*Face Palm*<br /><br />Final Score: The setting sucks, the writing sucks, the characters are irritating, the plot line is nonexistent, and It has only the most tenuous connection to the first two books. I honestly can't find a single redeeming quality for this book other than that at least it's short. Easily one of the worst books I've ever read, and I've read Chuck Wendig books.<br /><br />0/5</span>
  <a data-text-id="12450235601205772173" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('2j/E4DGEM83OOwbsQ8wtOH2YRSDP35OxA1AW7JtInxXOM+b6DuuO0rtS+05BghTiJBtlxmZhCoPxIq3oZvm1Zw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('4OxTEc7dkCwnzO2LFWppymeyBXNCMv1khksNwWRSUyf04HEL8bItM1KlECkXJFAQPjElleuMZFZ0ObbFmeN5VQ==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer18260812793383154524">Jeanne DuPrau spends several hours of every day at her computer, thinking up sentences. She has this quote taped to her wall: "A writer is someone for whom writing is harder than it is for other people" (Thomas Mann).<br/><br/>This gives her courage, because she finds writing very hard. So many words to choose from! So many different things that could happen in a story at any moment! Writing is one tough de</span>
  <span id="freeText18260812793383154524" style="display:none">Jeanne DuPrau spends several hours of every day at her computer, thinking up sentences. She has this quote taped to her wall: "A writer is someone for whom writing is harder than it is for other people" (Thomas Mann).<br /><br />This gives her courage, because she finds writing very hard. So many words to choose from! So many different things that could happen in a story at any moment! Writing is one tough decision after another.<br /><br />But it's also the most satisfying thing she knows how to do. So she keeps doing it. So far, she has written four novels, six books of nonfiction, and quite a few essays and stories.<br /><br />Jeanne DuPrau doesn't write every minute of every day. She also putters around in her garden. She lives in California, where it's easy to grow everything from apples to zinnias.<br /><br />Jeanne DuPrau doesn't have children, but she has two nephews, a niece, and a dog. The dog lives with her. His name is Ethan. Jeanne and Ethan get along well, though their interests are different. Ethan is not very fond of reading, for example, and Jeanne doesn't much like chasing squirrels. But they agree on walks, naps, and trips in the car to surprise destinations. Ethan also likes to help in the garden.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18260812793383154524" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
